  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ee2606aa-ca76-4fed-aede-c22337dbf8b7'
      });

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312608880" href="/book/show/7603179-comet-in-moominland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2168440553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7325093766954522820">[Note: Rating increased from 3 to 4 stars after reading the first moomin book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2187081651' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Moomins and the Great Flood</a>.]<br/><br/>Moomintroll’s quiet life is upended when foreboding images of a star with a tail send him journeying to speak with the Professors at the Observatory. Meeting new friends along the way and forging through perilous adventures together, Moomintroll and his companions arrive at the Observatory where they learn a comet is headed towards earth. Worse yet – the comet is predicted to land prec</span>
  <span id="freeText7325093766954522820" style="display:none">[Note: Rating increased from 3 to 4 stars after reading the first moomin book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2187081651" rel="nofollow noopener">The Moomins and the Great Flood</a>.]<br><br>Moomintroll’s quiet life is upended when foreboding images of a star with a tail send him journeying to speak with the Professors at the Observatory. Meeting new friends along the way and forging through perilous adventures together, Moomintroll and his companions arrive at the Observatory where they learn a comet is headed towards earth. Worse yet – the comet is predicted to land precisely where Moomintroll lives with his Moominpappa and Moominmamma. Moomintroll must find a quick way home if he’s going to warn his family in time. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509466767i/24324628._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="436" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s not difficult to see why ‘Moominmania’ exists. Jansson’s book conveys an innocence rarely found in modern titles. An undeniable charm exudes from her fanciful characters – the same type of odd yet memorable creatures one anticipates finding in an L. Frank Baum novel. <br><br>Moomins have a simple way of life. Their relaxed attitudes, gardens, and lovingly prepared meals are reminiscent of Tolkien’s hobbits. In fact, Jansson’s descriptions of the whimsical setting often invoke the sense that one is reading about an alternate Shire – a feeling made more robust by Moomintroll and his friends journeying to the Lonely Mountains. <br><br><i>Halfway up the hill on their way grew a clump of blue-trees covered with big yellow pears, and of course they couldn’t get past that without Sniff deciding that he was hungry.</i> <br><br><i>It certainly looked mysterious. Overhead the branches of the plum trees, oaks, and silver poplars met and formed a dark tunnel which led away into the unknown.</i> <br><br>Despite the impending threat of a comet hitting the earth, Moomintroll and his companions are relatively carefree. They remain (mostly) focused in their task to hurry home as they're shuffled from one peculiar instance to the next. The narrative lacks a sense of urgency, yet there’s something cathartic about the sweet simplicity of Moomintroll’s adventure. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509466767i/24324629._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="443" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sprinkled with darling illustrations, <i>Comet in Moominland</i> is a gentle tale of friendship and family.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7325093766954522820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_608792901" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/608792901" />
    <a title="Manny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1713956-manny"><img alt="Manny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442491692p2/1713956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/608792901?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manny" href="/user/show/1713956-manny">Manny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783401060958" href="/book/show/2994457-komet-im-mumintal">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who knows some German</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=well-i-think-its-funny">well-i-think-its-funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=german-and-dutch">german-and-dutch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=swedish-norwegian-and-danish">swedish-norwegian-and-danish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer608792901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5412770416274441475">As I've said many times on this site, I dislike translations on principle - but I am trying to do something about my miserable German, and when I saw this book at Foyles last week it immediately seemed like a good idea. I know the Swedish original well, and I figured that it should be easy to read and would improve my sketchy vocabulary. That worked out even better than I had hoped, and I already feel measurably more confident. <br/><br/>What surprised me, though, was that for once I experienced the trans</span>
  <span id="freeText5412770416274441475" style="display:none">As I've said many times on this site, I dislike translations on principle - but I am trying to do something about my miserable German, and when I saw this book at Foyles last week it immediately seemed like a good idea. I know the Swedish original well, and I figured that it should be easy to read and would improve my sketchy vocabulary. That worked out even better than I had hoped, and I already feel measurably more confident. <br /><br />What surprised me, though, was that for once I experienced the translation as utterly convincing. Not has been casting scorn on my claims here, and asking the obvious questions: given that my German is terrible, how can I know this is brilliant? But I just know. Even though I'm no good at the language, I have heard it spoken a great deal, and I understand how it's pronounced. I can hear it in my head when I'm reading, and it sounds exactly like the Swedish original. Everything is there. The rhythm of the narrative, with its ironic alternation of comedy and tragedy; the charming dialogues between the unforgettable characters; even the made-up names. It's a little miracle. The English translation is quite different. I can understand every word, rather than having to guess a quarter of them, but the soul of the book has disappeared. It isn't Tove Jansson any more.<br /><br />If you know German, and haven't read it already, get yourself a copy. It's just one of the best children's books ever written.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5412770416274441475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6097935694824703887">Moomin and Sniff explore a path which leads to the beach, they play, look at nature and find a cave, but they feel uneasy as they start to notice patterns carved into trees and objects, even seagulls arranged into the shape of a star with a tail.   <span id="freeText6097935694824703887" style="display:none">Moomin and Sniff explore a path which leads to the beach, they play, look at nature and find a cave, but they feel uneasy as they start to notice patterns carved into trees and objects, even seagulls arranged into the shape of a star with a tail. Moomin and Sniff set off on a journey to the observatory to find out what is happening.<br /><br />We really enjoyed the details in this story, and the ideas. Before reading this for the first time as a child I had never thought what the ocean floor would look like if the sea disappeared, or what you would do if a comet was coming towards the place where you live or what belongings you would take if you had to suddenly leave.<br /><br />As with all the Tove Jansson books we have read, we loved the relationships, the philosophy, the little creatures, the kindness and the reassuring safety of the moonin house that is there to come back to when your adventure is over.</span>

<div id="review_645558220" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/645558220" />
    <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira"><img alt="Ivonne Rovira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339470651p2/3803671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/645558220?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivonne Rovira" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira">Ivonne Rovira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780380004362" href="/book/show/2443903.Comet_in_Moominland_1">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">lovers of Pippi Longstocking, Beezus and Ramona, and other children's books that speak to adults</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3803671-ivonne-rovira?shelf=children-literature">children-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3803671-ivonne-rovira?shelf=children-classics">children-classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3803671-ivonne-rovira?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer645558220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7051774604236432505">How can it be that, unlike in the United Kingdom and the rest of Europe, the Moomin sagas never caught on in the United States? Finnish author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson' title='Tove Jansson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tove Jansson</a>'s tales of the white, hippo-like Moomintroll and his parents, Moominmamma and Moominpappa, would delight children and parents alike, the latter probably enjoying them even more, as adults can get the sly humor. I simply don't understand how Moominmania could possibly have bypassed the United States when it swept through Europe?<br/><br/><i>Comet in Moomin</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7051774604236432505" style="display:none">How can it be that, unlike in the United Kingdom and the rest of Europe, the Moomin sagas never caught on in the United States? Finnish author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson" title="Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">Tove Jansson</a>'s tales of the white, hippo-like Moomintroll and his parents, Moominmamma and Moominpappa, would delight children and parents alike, the latter probably enjoying them even more, as adults can get the sly humor. I simply don't understand how Moominmania could possibly have bypassed the United States when it swept through Europe?<br /><br /><i>Comet in Moominland</i>, the second in the series, follows Moomintroll; his rodent-like friend, the timid Sniff; and yet another pal, the clever tramp Snufkin, as they investigate the trajectory of a comet bound for Earth. Imagine their alarm when, after many adventures, they arrive at the Lonely Mountains and find out from the astronomers there that the comet will land in just four days' time!<br /><br />The band race back to Moominvalley to save the day -- and consult Moominmamma, as wise children do. With this gentle story, the outcome's never in doubt, but <i>Comet in Moominland</i> never descends to the saccharine -- far from it! I frequently laughed out loud at some of the snarky passages, especially involving Sniff's vying for credit and the young Moomintroll's bashful crush on the pretty Snork maiden.<br /><br />I'm going to try to read the entire series. Why should childhood be wasted only on the young?</span>
  <a data-text-id="7051774604236432505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789515005625" href="/book/show/4711309-kometen-kommer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=swedish-norwegian-and-danish">swedish-norwegian-and-danish</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer39027735" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10303475287015228572">A beautiful, ironic parody of the <i>Armageddon</i>-style killer meteorite movie, written before any of them existed. There are so many brilliant little details. I particularly loved the out-of-touch astronomers at the observatory, who have calculated exactly when the comet will strike ("possibly four seconds later," they add scrupulously), but seem completely uninterested by the fact that it will wipe out everyone in Moomin Valley. <br/><br/>In case you're worried, though, the Moomin family is more than a match</span>
  <span id="freeText10303475287015228572" style="display:none">A beautiful, ironic parody of the <i>Armageddon</i>-style killer meteorite movie, written before any of them existed. There are so many brilliant little details. I particularly loved the out-of-touch astronomers at the observatory, who have calculated exactly when the comet will strike ("possibly four seconds later," they add scrupulously), but seem completely uninterested by the fact that it will wipe out everyone in Moomin Valley. <br /><br />In case you're worried, though, the Moomin family is more than a match for one little rogue comet, and Moominpappa's wonderfully absurd solution saves the day. The writing in the original Swedish is impeccable; Jansson's unique blend of humor, melancholy and acute observation all comes together perfectly. I think this is her best book, and have read it several times. Suitable for anyone from eight to eighty-eight.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10303475287015228572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1922963119" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1922963119" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1922963119?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/34384350-komet-im-mumintal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=fairy-tales-fantasy">fairy-tales-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=favourites-read">favourites-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=translations">translations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1922963119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14595542936256531925">This here (and unfortunately also extremely rare and generally rather massively expensive if indeed even available used online) Ravensburger Taschenbücher German language translation of Tove Jansson's <u>Komet im Mumintal</u> (which Swedish language original title on the Goodreads database is <u>Kometer kommer</u>, although Vivica and Kurt Bandler's 1970 translation actually claims the original title to have been <u>Kometjakten</u>) was one of my favourite childhood reads (a book that I received in a large stack of </span>
  <span id="freeText14595542936256531925" style="display:none">This here (and unfortunately also extremely rare and generally rather massively expensive if indeed even available used online) Ravensburger Taschenbücher German language translation of Tove Jansson's <u>Komet im Mumintal</u> (which Swedish language original title on the Goodreads database is <u>Kometer kommer</u>, although Vivica and Kurt Bandler's 1970 translation actually claims the original title to have been <u>Kometjakten</u>) was one of my favourite childhood reads (a book that I received in a large stack of about twenty Ravensburger Taschenbücher as a birthday present in 1975, a book that I took with me when we immigrated to Canada in 1976 and that I even carried along in my trunk when I went to university in New Brunswick in 1985, where it unfortunately ended up somehow disappearing during one of those silly residence "panty raids" during frosh week, and oh boy, was I ever both sad and seriously, lastingly peeved at that). And honestly, to and for me personally, Vivica and Kurt Bandler's translation (and I finally did locate a reasonably intact and not too shabby copy online a couple of years ago) it still and absolutely feels as THE German language version of <u>Komet im Mumintal</u> I love the most, as the more recent translation by Birgitta Kicherer at least in my opinion leaves much to be desired and in particular that it fails to present far too many important details, such as for example patently ignoring the little silk monkey, who though strangely and incomprehensibly is still featured in Tove Jannsson's accompanying illustrations but textually seemingly forgotten by Kicherer (although according to readers who have read the original Swedish version, Kicherer supposedly does include parts that were left out by the Bandlers, but I for one simply cannot handle the removal of the silk monkey). And sorry, but with Elizabeth Portch's English language translation, with <u>Comet in Moominland</u> (which I did try and originally had quite high hopes for) her writing style, her narrational renderings expression and cadence wise, they just do not at least for me in any way capture the magic of the story, as they tend to make me feel aloof, above and beyond, and not really rooting for and exploring with Moomin, Sniff, Snuffkin and the rest of the group (but just dispassionately observing). <br /><br />However, while I do personally and always will prefer the Bandlers' 1970 German language translation, their <u>Komet im Mumintal</u>, I would still if recommending this second Moomin novel most definitely suggest Elizabeth Porch's English language translation, I would absolutely recommend <u>Comet in Moominland</u> before I would in any way even consider recommending Birgitta Kicherer's more recent German language translation, as the latter just really and frustratingly bothers me to on end with its additions and especially its subtractions and abridgements (and sorry, but even if it is indeed true that the recent German translation contains parts that appear in the Swedish original and do not appear in the 1970 translation, the little silk monkey has always been a favourite and I was seeing red so to speak when I could not find her textually in the Birgitta Kicherer translation). But if you do speak and read German and are indeed able to find Vivica and Kurt Bandler's 1970 Ravensburger Taschenbücher translation used, yes, consider reading their <u>Komet im Mumintal</u>, with its reddish and orange hued book cover of Moomin, Sniff, Snuffkin et al crossing the evaporated ocean on their stilts, as it truly is a lovely, evocative and fun, as well as occasionally eye-opening romp, a fantastical experience for young and old.<br /><br />Now with regard to content, what I love the most lastingly about <u>Komet im Mumintal</u> (and actually, this pertains to all of the Moomin books I have read so far) are the delightfully anecdotal episodes, which although generally complete in themselves also never feel as though they are hanging in space so to speak, as though there is not a thread of continuity from beginning to end, with the chapters seamlessly moving from the first inklings that a comet could perhaps be arriving to the fateful day it does (and how close the earth comes to disaster). But for me even more importantly (and probably the main reason why I have always so much adored the Moomin novels both as a child and now as an adult) I have so much appreciated how very much humanely and with personal understanding and supportiveness, Jansson describes and presents her diverse and often rather intriguing characters, and yes that even those individuals who show potentially problematic or negative behaviour patterns (such as Sniff, the Hemulens and even the silent, creepy Hattifatteners) are shown not only as negative but also with positiveness and much authorial understanding (and considering that the Hemulens, for example, with their OCD like obsessions and neuro-atypical ways and means could easily be considered as being on the autism spectrum, the Moomin books are in my humble opinion also interesting and important discussion vehicles, especially considering that these novels were for the most part penned at a time when autism and other such syndromes were not as yet really part of public awareness and the public conscience).</span>
  <a data-text-id="14595542936256531925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3734041" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3734041" />
    <a title="Suvi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59357-suvi"><img alt="Suvi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537657400p2/59357.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3734041?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suvi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suvi" href="/user/show/59357-suvi">Suvi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780374315269" href="/book/show/1369890.Comet_in_Moominland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=_book-shelf">_book-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=1940-1969">1940-1969</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=_europe-northern">_europe-northern</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3734041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1218129466816559151"><b>Re-read 02.04.2020</b><br/>No change in rating.<br/><br/><b>15.06.2014</b><br/>Like so many Finnish children of a certain generation, I grew up watching the <i>Moomins</i> tv-series (there are still reruns every once in a while, and the magic has never faded) and visited <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moomin_World' rel='nofollow noopener'>Moomin World</a>. Now, to honor Tove Jansson's centenary, I started a project of reading all her Moomin books. Maybe the rest of her body of work as well, if I have the time or enthusiasm.<br/><br/>When the 1992 animated movie premiered in Finland, my mom took me to see it. The p</span>
  <span id="freeText1218129466816559151" style="display:none"><b>Re-read 02.04.2020</b><br />No change in rating.<br /><br /><b>15.06.2014</b><br />Like so many Finnish children of a certain generation, I grew up watching the <i>Moomins</i> tv-series (there are still reruns every once in a while, and the magic has never faded) and visited <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moomin_World" rel="nofollow noopener">Moomin World</a>. Now, to honor Tove Jansson's centenary, I started a project of reading all her Moomin books. Maybe the rest of her body of work as well, if I have the time or enthusiasm.<br /><br />When the 1992 animated movie premiered in Finland, my mom took me to see it. The part where Muskrat sits on the cake was funny, but mostly the oppressive mood stayed with me. I don't remember the happy ending, but I do remember the part where creatures big and small were hurrying away from Moominvalley with all their possessions, the frantic search for the kitten, and the red sky that reminded of the impending doom.<br /><br />The book is very similar to the movie with minor differences (the change of the chump Silk Monkey into a kitten worked better in my opinion), and has echoes of nuclear explosions and their scorching power to destroy everything. Everyone in the valley has their way of surviving in the middle of an increasing dread of an uncertain future. Moominmamma just keeps going with her chores and bakes a cake, but Moomintroll and Sniff travel to the Observatory of the Lonely Mountains to find out more about the approaching comet. On their journey they meet other familiar characters who join the Moomin family.<br /><br />The contrast between them all works great (Sniff is a selfish whiner, the fickle Snork Maiden is vain and loves beautiful things, and the practical Snork is obsessed about details and having meetings about everything). There's a little of them in all of us. Snufkin is my favorite, and here we meet him for the first time. He sees beauty even in the starkest of sceneries and proves to be a great asset to the group with his experience in adventures.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"It was a funny little path, winding here and there, dashing off in different directions, and sometimes even tying a knot in itself from sheer joy. (You don't get tired of a path like that, and I'm not sure that it doesn't get you home quicker in the end."</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="1218129466816559151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/343944-emily?shelf=my-happy-childhood">my-happy-childhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/343944-emily?shelf=read-aloud">read-aloud</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59191404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11316096234324100171">Just revisited this book for the first time in a long while by reading it aloud to my 6 year-old. Two main thoughts:<br/><br/>1. I love Tove Jansson. She always writes with a slightly off-beat charm (one of my favorite bits in this book is the title of the butterfly collecting Hemulin's book, <i> Moths of the Eastern Hemisphere: their Behavior and Misbehavior</i>) and her stories tend to swing uneasily between the surreal (Hattifatteners, anyone?) and the comforting (coffee and cake), a style which I found somew</span>
  <span id="freeText11316096234324100171" style="display:none">Just revisited this book for the first time in a long while by reading it aloud to my 6 year-old. Two main thoughts:<br /><br />1. I love Tove Jansson. She always writes with a slightly off-beat charm (one of my favorite bits in this book is the title of the butterfly collecting Hemulin's book, <i> Moths of the Eastern Hemisphere: their Behavior and Misbehavior</i>) and her stories tend to swing uneasily between the surreal (Hattifatteners, anyone?) and the comforting (coffee and cake), a style which I found somewhat confusing as a child, but came to adore when I reread the books in college. However, this is one of her earliest books, and it shows. After Moomintroll and his friends learn that a comet is threatening the earth, they travel to an observatory to learn more about it. Much of the story consists of them encountering one peril after another on their long journey. It gets a little repetitive, and that contributes to a general flatness and lack of emotional depth to this book. Also there's some rather tedious gender stereotyping in the relationship between Moomintroll and the Snork Maiden -- even as a child, I thought the Snork Maiden was overdoing the damsel in distress act. But I can forgive Jansson all this for the wonderful chapter about crossing the dried up sea on stilts.<br /><br />2. This perhaps was not the best choice of book to read aloud to a child who is already prone to fanatsizing and worring about calamatous events, such as the sun blowing up. But I told him it had a happy ending (that's not a spoiler, right? I mean we know they're not wiped out by the comet because of all the sequels), and he enjoyed it a lot, and I loved reading it aloud. We are ready to start <i>Finn Family Moomintroll</i>!<br /><br />ETA: Days after finishing this, I've decided to change my review to four stars, because despite its flaws the book has stuck with me, and the writing was so lovely and the penultimate chapter so exciting. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11316096234324100171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_80178943" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80178943" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1433865-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1254324661p2/1433865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80178943?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/1433865-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140302868" href="/book/show/222603.Comet_in_Moominland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1433865-robert?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80178943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4265344159467187661">The Moomins, a family of trolls, have appeared in my life in various ways; I vaguely remember having read (or having been read) one of the novels as a young child - as an older child I remember the animated series on television. I happened across it by accident and spent much time in enjoyable confusion about the names and natures of the seemingly infinite cast of characters. This year I decided I wanted to find out more than my hazy memories could tell me and in the process stumbled across the </span>
  <span id="freeText4265344159467187661" style="display:none">The Moomins, a family of trolls, have appeared in my life in various ways; I vaguely remember having read (or having been read) one of the novels as a young child - as an older child I remember the animated series on television. I happened across it by accident and spent much time in enjoyable confusion about the names and natures of the seemingly infinite cast of characters. This year I decided I wanted to find out more than my hazy memories could tell me and in the process stumbled across the fact that Tove Jansson had written and drawn a Moomin strip comic for a British newspaper and I acquired the first volume of the collected strip comics and read it. I was pleasantly surprised to find it densely but gently satirical as well as pleased to find that the bizarre imagination (particularly for characters who are mythic or completely invented creatures) was most definitely as I recalled.<br /><br />This meant I still didn't know what the novels were like, but encouraged by the high quality of the comic strip and my memories, I decided to give Comet in Moominland a go - selected because it was the first written (though not first published, I think) of the Moomin novels. <br /><br />It turned out to be a delightful, pleasant book, strong on imagined characters and incidental mystery - what is a Snufkin? Just how much difference is there between a Troll and a Snork? Everybody and everything is introduced blithely as if common-place without any real requirement for detailed explanation. Everybody knows what a Hattifattener is, really - description is almost superfluous.<br /><br />The plot is epic compared to those in the volume of comic strips I read - the fate of Moomin Valley (and the rest of the world, really) is at stake and an arduous journey is undertaken to request knowledge and help in saving the day.<br /><br />The gentle satire is present but in lesser quantity - a philosopher who states that everything is Unnecessary, is never-the-less rather keen on creature comforts (all the more so because he is a creature - a Muskrat)and not being destroyed by the impact of a celstial body. Not keen enough to actually help avert the crisis, however. The scientists that Moomintroll appeals to for information and help take no interest, but pour out all their knowledge to the Snork Maiden when asked about their work...<br /><br />Contrast of characters is also used to give a Message about the moral and physical dangers of too much attachment to physical belongings (a sentiment expressed in the comic strip, too). The characters are also used to promote the virtues of friendship and familial love. Moomintroll's faith that his mother, Moominmama will fix everything if only they can get back to her in time, is touching - hasn't there been a time in all our lives when we had absolute faith that Mum could resolve any problem satisfactorily? <br /><br />I suppose it is not too much of a spoiler to reveal that Moomintroll, friends and family, The Valley of the Moomins and even the rest of the planet survive to return in more books; I look forward to reading them.<br /><br />I would say that comparing Comic Strip vol.1 to Novel 1, the strip has just a slight edge in my opinion because it is more densely packed with satire, but that a greater focus on plot is suited to the novel as a form, so perhaps each should be enjoyed for their own merits and comparison should not be dwelled on too much.<br /><br />Now, if only some-one would tell me what order the rest of the novels are meant to be read in....<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4265344159467187661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1435613848" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1054174147659046769">Tove Jansson is a genius! Her humor is always understated and overdone -- a unique absurdist matter of fact emotionally evasive and, of course, refreshingly direct, marshmallowy slapstick. <br/><br/>"I can't leave my imperial snorks to the comet!" <br/><br/>I so love the ghost in this one, and the dance, the heroic tree-climbing incident, and the moving of things to "safer places." The disappearing ocean, the pisciculturist, his screaming shrimp, and the fantastic finale. <br/><br/>Jansson makes terrible fun of dramatic tens</span>
  <span id="freeText1054174147659046769" style="display:none">Tove Jansson is a genius! Her humor is always understated and overdone -- a unique absurdist matter of fact emotionally evasive and, of course, refreshingly direct, marshmallowy slapstick. <br /><br />"I can't leave my imperial snorks to the comet!" <br /><br />I so love the ghost in this one, and the dance, the heroic tree-climbing incident, and the moving of things to "safer places." The disappearing ocean, the pisciculturist, his screaming shrimp, and the fantastic finale. <br /><br />Jansson makes terrible fun of dramatic tension and scientists, and, I'm pretty sure, humans (we are ridiculous). There is an eerie and beautiful foreboding and, as always, joke after joke after off-beat joke. <br /><br />Always a good way to start the weekend.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1054174147659046769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3479384712259653219">The Moomin books are always deceptively simple. I love how Jansson balances the matter-of-fact and the bizarre, and always constructs her stories with her characters front and centre, with all their flaws and quirks and earnest humanity. I always feel like I've learned some big things after reading these. I was especially interested in checking this one out as I hadn't read it before, and it's the first appearance of Snufkin, who is in a lot of ways my favourite character.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11700014675791532409">Well, well, well. A while back, I was originally wary about starting this book because I thought the idea was weird for a children's book. (A comet about to destroy the world.) Comets destroying the world are on my top ten "Scary" list....<br/><br/>Anyway, after months of forgetting about this book and then remembering it, I don't know what made me start it after surving a huge earthquake in real life. (Not very smart of me.) I think that somehow (despite the title) I forgot it was about a comet hurtling </span>
  <span id="freeText11700014675791532409" style="display:none">Well, well, well. A while back, I was originally wary about starting this book because I thought the idea was weird for a children's book. (A comet about to destroy the world.) Comets destroying the world are on my top ten "Scary" list....<br /><br />Anyway, after months of forgetting about this book and then remembering it, I don't know what made me start it after surving a huge earthquake in real life. (Not very smart of me.) I think that somehow (despite the title) I forgot it was about a comet hurtling toward earth. It has some scary parts. It reminded me of the movie "Armageddon". Sort of. But it is basically a funny book. (Other than the end of the world parts.) <br /><br />I read "Finn Family Moomintroll" a long time ago and was VERY confused about the characters and I should have read this first because it introduces all the wacky creatures. There also may be a book about a great flood---this book keeps mentioning it. (???) Comets, floods .... Oh, and this book has a tornado, too. But really it is a funny book! I promise! Despite the fact that they might all die!<br /><br />I think I am ready for some Junie B. Jones now. (Funny, but without any comets.)</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1606583192" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17380228161359920802">Why am I so late coming to the Moomins? I must have been crazy. First I loved the comic strips <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/79548.Moomin_The_Complete_Tove_Jansson_Comic_Strip__Vol__1' title='Moomin The Complete Tove Jansson Comic Strip, Vol. 1 by Tove Jansson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Moomin: The Complete Tove Jansson Comic Strip, Vol. 1</a> and now, with Tove's second Moomin novel read, I have found that I adore her written work as much as her illustrations. <br/>Comet in Moominland involves Moomintroll, Sniff and Snufkin (my fav.) going on an adventure to try and solve the mystery of the looming comet making its way towards earth. They encounter many weird and wonderful creatures on their </span>
  <span id="freeText17380228161359920802" style="display:none">Why am I so late coming to the Moomins? I must have been crazy. First I loved the comic strips <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/79548.Moomin_The_Complete_Tove_Jansson_Comic_Strip__Vol__1" title="Moomin The Complete Tove Jansson Comic Strip, Vol. 1 by Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">Moomin: The Complete Tove Jansson Comic Strip, Vol. 1</a> and now, with Tove's second Moomin novel read, I have found that I adore her written work as much as her illustrations. <br />Comet in Moominland involves Moomintroll, Sniff and Snufkin (my fav.) going on an adventure to try and solve the mystery of the looming comet making its way towards earth. They encounter many weird and wonderful creatures on their journey until they bump headlong into Moonmintroll's beloved Snork maiden and her brother. Can they make it back to safety before the comet strikes?<br /><br />It's difficult to capture, at the moment, the huge appeal and love I feel for these stories. There is a great sense of love and family which is central to the narrative yet each character is SO individual in their traits throughout that you believe they are as real as the person reading them. </span>

<div id="review_1803955045" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1803955045" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2631425-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538808870p2/2631425.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1803955045?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/2631425-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312608880" href="/book/show/7603179-comet-in-moominland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2631425-michael?shelf=illustrated">illustrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2631425-michael?shelf=no-longer-own">no-longer-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2631425-michael?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1803955045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer865296486561571249">A fantastical, whimsical, comical, almost tragical adventure in which Moomintroll is involved in a child's-eye-view of the impending apocalypse. Along the way, he meets strange characters, some of whom will become beloved friends of both the Moomins and the reader (Snufkin, I'm talking about you!).<br/><br/>It's no spoiler - there's another seven books in the series - to say that everything turns out OK. The enjoyment is in the journey and the heroic and cowardly antics of the Moomins and friends and, for</span>
  <span id="freeText865296486561571249" style="display:none">A fantastical, whimsical, comical, almost tragical adventure in which Moomintroll is involved in a child's-eye-view of the impending apocalypse. Along the way, he meets strange characters, some of whom will become beloved friends of both the Moomins and the reader (Snufkin, I'm talking about you!).<br /><br />It's no spoiler - there's another seven books in the series - to say that everything turns out OK. The enjoyment is in the journey and the heroic and cowardly antics of the Moomins and friends and, for children and adults alike, a comfort in returning to the warm bosom of Moominmamma at the end.<br /><br />Jansson's illustrations are superb, of course, being an integral part of the story and its tone, which can be rather grotesque at times - the stiltwalkers put me in mind of Dali's <i>Temptation of St Anthony</i>. A bold image for a children's book, and there are others just as eschatological. Despite which, the overall tone is not at all bleak, rather the opposite.</span>
  <a data-text-id="865296486561571249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3208922554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3208922554" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5129776-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331301021p2/5129776.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3208922554?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/5129776-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780241344477" href="/book/show/37119752-comet-in-moominland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5129776-chris?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5129776-chris?shelf=moomins">moomins</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3208922554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12947544218993270318">A visitor from space is hurtling towards Moominland but it isn't friendly, in fact it could cause devastation. Young Moomintroll and his friend Sniff set off to an observatory on a mountain to find out exactly when and where the comet will land.<br/><br/><em>Comet in Moominland</em> is therefore a tale of their expedition -- but it is not really all about that, for Jansson's story is, as all good stories are, about the people involved and their relationships with each other.<br/><br/>For those, like me, faintly familiar or </span>
  <span id="freeText12947544218993270318" style="display:none">A visitor from space is hurtling towards Moominland but it isn't friendly, in fact it could cause devastation. Young Moomintroll and his friend Sniff set off to an observatory on a mountain to find out exactly when and where the comet will land.<br /><br /><em>Comet in Moominland</em> is therefore a tale of their expedition -- but it is not really all about that, for Jansson's story is, as all good stories are, about the people involved and their relationships with each other.<br /><br />For those, like me, faintly familiar or even strangers to the Moomin tales, it was an adventure in itself to meet with Moomintroll, his family, Sniff, a muskrat, a silk monkey, Snufkin, some Hemulen and others, all with their characteristics and idiosyncrasies.<br /><br />I have to confess that I never understood the fuss made of the Moomins: I thought they looked sweet, even charming, but I hadn't fallen under their spell, and I was dubious that I would after a few chapters.<br /><br />And then something magical happened. Instead of a series of chapters with only loosely related incidents, what began to emerge was a picture of relationships. Some of these were close, others a bit fraught; but here were a bunch of disparate creatures thrown together by chance and circumstances who managed to rub along together.<br /><br />Moomintroll, his family and the related Snorks are friendly cuddly animals, like furry hippos but without the aggression; Sniff is like a hybrid kangaroo rabbit but with short legs; the Hemulen are dour figures with big snouts and shapeless robes; Snufkin is a tramp with a big hat, shepherd's smock and a mouth organ; but essentially these are all human children in disguise. There are humans as such, but the astronomers (grumpy to a man) and the woman in the village shop all refer to the assorted expeditioners as 'children', an indication of how we should regard the inhabitants of this world and with whom young readers (and not so young readers) might choose to identify.<br /><br />The narrative takes Moomintroll and Sniff through a sequence of landscapes, first through woods to a seashore ringed with cliffs, later on a raft along an increasingly perilous river, up mountains and back across deserts and a terrain from which all water has disappeared. And all through the September and early October days the comet is getting nearer, the sky redder, the atmosphere hotter. Yet the underlying message -- if message there is -- seems to be that it is necessary to take risks, to see what one is capable of, but that there is always the expectation of a loving family to come home to.<br /><br />Was I charmed? Did I fall under the Moomin spell? I must confess that I suspect I was, and that I'm grateful to all the urgings to try the series and indeed to begin with this, the second of the series of nine. And, as well as the humour, not a little of the enchantment came from Jansson's delightful, delicate line drawings, and especially the scenic landscapes, which one has only to view to fall for, with their vistas and skies drawing the gaze. I'm now contemplating what title should now follow this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12947544218993270318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_111372439" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111372439" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112377-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217926616p2/112377.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111372439?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/112377-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112377-kim?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112377-kim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111372439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13061195941020458855">Hooray, my library seems to be getting in the new editions of the Moomin books! So you can expect more reviews of them from me by and by.<br/><br/><i>Comet in Moominland</i> was the first full-length Moomin novel, published nearly 65 years ago. (The very first Moomin book, <i>The Moomins and the Great Flood</i> came out in 1945, so the Moomins celebrate their 65th anniversary this year.) The Moomin books in general are self-contained enough that the reader can start with any one of them, however, <i>Comet in Moominland</i> in</span>
  <span id="freeText13061195941020458855" style="display:none">Hooray, my library seems to be getting in the new editions of the Moomin books! So you can expect more reviews of them from me by and by.<br /><br /><i>Comet in Moominland</i> was the first full-length Moomin novel, published nearly 65 years ago. (The very first Moomin book, <i>The Moomins and the Great Flood</i> came out in 1945, so the Moomins celebrate their 65th anniversary this year.) The Moomin books in general are self-contained enough that the reader can start with any one of them, however, <i>Comet in Moominland</i> introduces many of the family characters in the series, including the Snork Siblings and Snufkin, who will go on to become some of Moomintroll's closest friends. <br /><br />When he finds out a comet is approaching, a panic-stricken Moomintroll decides to find out as much about it as he can, so he and his friend Sniff set off for an observatory high in the mountains. Along the way, they meet with many dangers and new friends, and find out that the comet is heading for Moominvalley itself. Can they get back in time to warn their family and friends?<br /><br />There are so many things to like about the Moomin books. They are whimsical fantasies peopled with cute and unusual creatures, yet the characters' thoughts, feelings, and behavior are familiar and believable. Throughout <i>Comet</i>, for instance, no matter how scary things get, Moomintroll has faith that his father knows how to fix everything, and that his mother can make everything right. Young children really do think like that. And when Snufkin tells the others of the Snorks, who look just like Moomins but change color with their emotions, Moomintroll is scornful, especially of the lovely Snork Maiden. But he shifts very quickly from feeling threatened by her to talking about nothing else, before the two of them have even met. I must admit, their relationship was one of the things I liked most about the story, as it had all the charm and innocence of first love. It didn't hurt that they took turns rescuing one another, and that while the Snork Maiden is very girly and slightly vain, she is also quite clever and resourceful. No wonder Moomintroll is smitten!<br /><br />If you have children in need of a bedtime story, you have an excellent excuse to pick up the Moomin books. But if you are simply an adult with a childlike sense of wonder, you're sure to be charmed by them as well.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13061195941020458855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1843839792639831652"><b>My review was first posted on <a href='https://northernplunder.wordpress.com/2018/07/20/book-review-comet-in-moominland/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Northern Plunder</a>, you can read <a href='https://northernplunder.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>more of my reviews there too</a>.</b><br/><br/>Comet in Moominland was a present from my lovely Finnish friend Tecsie along with some other good from Finland.<br/><br/>I had intended to read it straight away but I ended up being very lucky as it won the vote for Books and Tea’s read-along for January.<br/><br/>I don’t read a whole lot of Middle Grade books but I’ve seen a lot of art of the Moomin characters and was pretty excited to start it.<br/><br/>Comet in Moominland is listed a</span>
  <span id="freeText1843839792639831652" style="display:none"><b>My review was first posted on <a href="https://northernplunder.wordpress.com/2018/07/20/book-review-comet-in-moominland/" rel="nofollow noopener">Northern Plunder</a>, you can read <a href="https://northernplunder.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">more of my reviews there too</a>.</b><br /><br />Comet in Moominland was a present from my lovely Finnish friend Tecsie along with some other good from Finland.<br /><br />I had intended to read it straight away but I ended up being very lucky as it won the vote for Books and Tea’s read-along for January.<br /><br />I don’t read a whole lot of Middle Grade books but I’ve seen a lot of art of the Moomin characters and was pretty excited to start it.<br /><br />Comet in Moominland is listed as the second book in the series on Goodreads but my copy has #1 on the side so figure that one out? ahah.<br /><br />Either way it doesn’tt really effect the reading order, there is mention that a Great Flood happened before this book starts but that is about it.<br /><br />This book follows Moomintroll and his friends as they travel very far to speak to some scientist to find out more about the Comet that is on its way to destroy the valley.<br /><br />I really enjoyed reading this adventure because the world that is created is very vivid with its description and little illustrations to go along.<br /><br />I also think the way the characters interacted was great too as small children will definitely relate to how Moomintroll is – ready to impress, eager to be the leader, but also scared because there is still so much he doesn’t know yet.<br /><br />On top of this he’s also really cute because he’s insistant that girls aren’t worth his time, but the moment he meets Snork Maiden he can’t wait to impress her and give her pretty things. So cute.<br /><br />If you’re not big into middle grade books I’d probably say this might not be for you as the writing style and sentence structure is definitely geared more towards that age range – as expected.<br /><br />Its a super fun read but its unlikely I’ll go out of my way to read the rest of the series.</span>

  <span id="freeText15590681548942060610" style="display:none">I remember having a Spanish copy of this book but somehow I never got to read it and only watched the animated movie from 1992, then I lost that copy and although I enjoyed the movie I remember it didn't become one of my favorite Moomin stories, so I forgot about the book and read other Jansson's works before finally getting a copy again.<br /><br />Aaaand... this was awesome. I'm actually glad it took me this long to read it because I was able to experience a Moomin story for the first time again (I had already forgotten all the details). It is not quite as dark as the last books in the series (my favorites), but it made me laugh and think and get excited, and seeing the characters I already know interact for the first time was great, as well as going with them on this adventure.<br /><br />So, yeah, I love Tove Jansson and I can't wait for my niece to grow up so she can enjoy the Moomin series as much as I do (hopefully) &lt;3</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4479095631869407195">I have heard of the Moomins because I keep running across them on blogs. People love the Moomins. It turns out the stories were written in the 40s and 50s by a Finnish author. I discovered a Moomin memorabilia display and a handful of her books for sale at a store in the Twin Cities and I decided I needed to explore. After all, one of my favorite authors is Astrid Lindgren and she was Swedish... it turns out that Lindgren and Jansson have something in common. They both have a remarkable wit and </span>
  <span id="freeText4479095631869407195" style="display:none">I have heard of the Moomins because I keep running across them on blogs. People love the Moomins. It turns out the stories were written in the 40s and 50s by a Finnish author. I discovered a Moomin memorabilia display and a handful of her books for sale at a store in the Twin Cities and I decided I needed to explore. After all, one of my favorite authors is Astrid Lindgren and she was Swedish... it turns out that Lindgren and Jansson have something in common. They both have a remarkable wit and wonder and manage to capture my attention. I can't decide who I love more in this book: Sniff, Snufkin, the Hemulens, Moomintroll, Snork, the Snork Maiden, or any of the other enchanting characters. If you like the quirky characters found in Wind in the Willows or Winnie the Pooh, you just might love these ones too. I need to read them all.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13260736370657764111">Second reading of this one, and I still don't love it. Looking back at my comments from 2011 (from a different edition, and GR won't let me combine them), I see "cute but not compelling." This time, perhaps because I've read the whole series now, even the "cute" has worn off. I can see the "social commentary" that people mention, but it has no depth, and I don't like any of the characters except the philosophical muskrat, who is an Eeyore figure, and the Moomin parents, who are only bit players </span>
  <span id="freeText13260736370657764111" style="display:none">Second reading of this one, and I still don't love it. Looking back at my comments from 2011 (from a different edition, and GR won't let me combine them), I see "cute but not compelling." This time, perhaps because I've read the whole series now, even the "cute" has worn off. I can see the "social commentary" that people mention, but it has no depth, and I don't like any of the characters except the philosophical muskrat, who is an Eeyore figure, and the Moomin parents, who are only bit players in this book. And, just to demonstrate that my complaints are due to my Not being the intended audience, my kids both upped their ratings from "4" to "5" stars this time round. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ue5r68xNQYY8kfDfY5VWHsYX17fBqx4DOje/2ID2euZJjQ9BOcGSHwc85AG6LQiAboRzLaMs+rSd6fH6Ssom7g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('svWfK2RIeSoOcLWNNsOq1g2f/0lznTKLJO5bb3s60eKqlvuBkcSqszXdoVPve/RIpQxb0xEa1jyDMBVNsQaN6g==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11798772749857660069"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br/><br/>Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br/><br/>Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> </span>
  <span id="freeText11798772749857660069" style="display:none"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br /><br />Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br /><br />Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3300083-the-moomins-and-the-great-flood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Moomins and the Great Flood</a> (1945), during World War II. She said later that the war had depressed her, and she had wanted to write something naive and innocent. Besides the <i>Moomin</i> novels and short stories, Tove Jansson also wrote and illustrated four original and highly popular picture books.<br /><br />Jansson's <i>Moomin</i> books have been translated into 33 languages. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11798772749857660069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
